< Review>
They had the food ready on time. The food is great. We had the chicken Tika masala, alu Gobi, lamb korma, nav rattan korma, chicken tandoori, vegetable samosas, garlic and regular Naan. Yumm! If you use grubhub via yelp, keep in mind that when you order the curries, you have a choice to get rice (whole plate) or naan (few pieces). We ended up with a lot of rice and not as much naan.< /Review>

<gmap_id>0x80dbf92a25067d23:0x4f9c5bc174a59e5f<//gmap_id><name>S.K. Roy</name>< Review>
Ashoka makes a tasty curry chicken dish. It's my favorite. The pieces of chicken (bone-in) are soft, moist, and flavorful. HOWEVER, the bones are not sliced cleanly. They are fragmented at the edges into dangerous splinters, and one has to spit them out while eating -- and some splinters are so small they are swallowed.

One person in my family broke a tooth on a bone fragment, and it's only a matter of time before one of these bone splinters perforates someone's intestine and a lawsuit is filed against the restaurant. That would be a shame, since the food is delicious. If they chop the meat themselves, I strongly suggest they find a professional butcher instead. If they already use a professional butcher, it's time to change to another one. A delicious meal is not worth an expensive trip to the ER or the dental surgeon.

No other restaurant I've visited (of any ethnicity) that serves bone-in chicken leaves bone splinters in the dish. Surely this situation can be improved.

I hope the owners/cooks at Ashoka are reading this. PLEASE, no more bone fragments!< /Review>

< Text>
This is more of the temple/church for Laos and Thais.
Thais and some cultural classes offer on Wednesday and Sunday.  On Sunday you can get many hard to find vegetables and ingredients from the local growers at very good price. Also, on Sunday and you can get very cheap and authentic Thai food too. I bought Thai BBQ chicken on a stick and sticky rice for only $2.00 each. Hard to find parking.<//Text>

<GmapID>0x80dbf37f11c205af:0x7a7753cfd20fdfe1</GmapID><Text>None< /Text><user_id>116897234845586849081</user_id><rating>5< /rating>< username>

<time>1620157772335</time><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Text>I've had take out from this place at least once a week for the last 6 months

There's definitely some issues to discuss. Is there good cooking here? Well, it's certainly possible. There's been times where've thought it was pleasant enough. But the truth of the matter is, Mountain View has always been a dead spot for good Chinese cooking, and if you need proof, just walk down Castro street.

Dumpling Garden is a restaurant where there are moments. Moments where the food is fine, especially as they are comparatively more affordable compared to other Chinese restaurants in the area.

The issue is primarily in the lack of consistency and the clear evidence of skimping. If you order the pan fried dumpling, you'll find yourself biting into the air as only 1/3 - 1/5 of the dumpling has any protein stuffing. If you order take out soup dumplings, they'll conveniently forget the vinegar and chili or the chopsticks. The Thai tea will taste of 25% sugar and taste muted.

Off memory, in the last 6 months, you will more often come across at least one notable issue that diminishes the flavor of the meal. It never feels like there's intent to make the food taste poorly, but there is a feeling of nickel and dime-ing.

Maybe the dine-in experience is better, but the take-out leaves much to be desired.< /Text>< response>
None< /response>

B. Li<//user_name>
<GmapID>0x808fb0a4549331c5:0x4b5726dd50b48da3< /GmapID><Rating>2<//Rating></record>

< Review>
Stumbled upon this place looking for somewhere to eat after a trip to Walmart. My family loves dumplings and we're always on the hunt for good places to eat while in other cities.

We ordered a few typical dishes we would to compare to our local dumpling spot. The marinated pig ears were nice and tender with good flavor. The mustard green soup was okay. It wasn't hot, but the beef was good.

We also got lamb with Napa cabbage dumplings as well as for and chive. Both were delicious.

Prices were about $3 more per dish than what I'm used to, but it's not too bad considering I didn't see another dumpling spot in the area.<//Review>

<text>Dumpling garden used to be really bad but they have recently revamped everything and it is now a lot better! Some dishes I've tried:

- Spicy boiled fish: Their best dish imo. Really nicely seasoned fish filets, perfect amount of spicy vs savory. Fish is tender, and there is a lot of it compared to veggies. Also has wood ear mushrooms which I personally really like.
- Cucumber wood ear mushroom salad: Not bad but missing vinegar or some kind of acid. Sauce is soy sauce and garlic basically.
- Bok choy with garlic: pretty good! Has nice wok hei.
- Roast five spice chicken: Better than expected in terms of flavor. It has a super dry five spice flavor, and the dish is served cold. It is kind of in the style of chicken jerky as the chicken is pretty dry but that's just the style. Don't expect juicy chicken though.
- Chow mein: It's fine, but it's not seasoned well enough and personally wouldn't get this again.
- 3 flavor dumplings: Tastes similar to frozen dumplings you can get at 99 ranch. Aka, not too bad but nothing special.
- lotus root salad: I don't really like this as the lotus isn't very fresh and the flavor is very one note (basically salt).<//text><pictures>None</pictures><Resp>None<//Resp>< GmapID>

<text>Hands down the best place to throw a kid party!

Our 5-year-old loves open play at this place. So naturally we knew Imagine Me Grow would be the perfect place to throw our youngest daughter's 1st birthday party. And boy were we right! It was completely stress-free and there was no mess to clean up afterwards.

We were allowed to bring in our own food/decorations; however, you can also purchase them through Imagine Me Grow. But regardless, the staff, which by the way, were the sweetest, helped set up our party decor and food/dessert stations. Oh, and they even took photos as well!

Also, most kid party centers do not allow you to bring in your own food so this was a major plus for us as our oldest has a couple severe food allergies.

But the best part of it all was that all of our guests had an amazing time. Everyone kept complimenting how fun and cute the place was. Some even mentioned they'd like to throw their next kids birthday party there.</text>< pics>

<Pics>None< /Pics>< Text>
Wonderful fun play stations! We attended a birthday party here today for a classmate of my son. 4/5 year olds and their siblings were welcomed and allowed to play and explore. It reminded me of a  children's pottery barn catalog brought to life! Very sweet moments as my son and friends served one another in the bakery and sea food restaurant. My younger two loved the fire station very much. The cars can be pushed around the road and this was a please t surprise. The dance room was often empty but once in a while the children would enter and burst into dance. It was fun! Each room has a small screen tv with the rooms topic playing on the screen. At first I felt this was unecessary but as the party progressed it made sense, and had no sound so it wasn't intrusive to their imaginative play.

A music room would be fun, but trust me the kids were very satisfied and the play kitchens, fire station and dance room seemed to be my three boys favorite.

If I had to give any critique it would be to share that it is not a tactile/sensory experience as it is very clean and free of any sand or water play. That is understandable as it accomadates cooperative play amongst many children, young children. The environment fostered cooperative play and surprisingly allowed children the freedom to cooperate and play individually. I highly recommend!

In a time where children play centers resemble casinos and bars, and are often filled with video games this was refreshing!

Created for the younger child I find it sweet that they are not bombarded with flashing lights and bribery of candy and cheap toys. If my older kids were with me I could see them getting a little "bored" but I would encourage them to play and pretend with their younger siblings and I know the entire family would be better for it! So often we spend time and money to celebrate our children but we end up just consuming and teaching them greed and consuming. This truly fosters imaginative play that will help families bond, social skills flourish and develop life long memories.</Text>

<Text>Very good selection of great tasting frozen yogurt. Stopped in yesterday while letting my grandson play in the water feature out front (yes, that's its purpose). The selection was great with typical lighter summer flavors. I opted for the watermelon and dole pineapple. Typically, I've found almost every frozen yogurt place makes the watermelon very tart, this wasn't the case here. Paired very well with the pineapple and added some yogurt chips for a little texture and neutral sweet punch. Their fruit toppings looked a bit less pleasant, so I skipped on those. All in all I'd say they're a 4 star easy.. Clean, great flavors and priced right.< /Text><username>Doc Chop<//username>< pictures>

<review>After finding myself in the beautiful Canyon Crest Towne Centre, while appraising some of the local parks in the area, I stumbled across this indigenous froyo vendor.  Looking too cute to pass up, I inspected the flavors on tap, and was stunned to get an eyefull of Green Apple.  I've never come across anyone else brazen enough to flaunt this tart tang.

So I loaded up a small ole cup with pomegranate, tart, mango and green apple... topping it with my favorite dry cereal from a long running cartoon series... yes, Fruity Pebbles.  I normally carry a baggie in my pocket, but today I had my Hawaiian swim trunks on, because I was going jogging at the park, and had forgotten my awkwardly small compression shorts in the next state.

But my lavish topping splurge didn't stop there.  I also adorned my dessert with fresh blueberries, sliced strawberries and kiwi, some mochi and topped it off with a maraschino cherry... which I topped with a single raspberry... which I then topped with a dollop of raspberry syrup.  Genius!

After I gingerly placed my creation onto the scale, the sales associate asked me if I cared to guess the price before tax, which if assessed properly, would allow me to walk out without paying one red cent (plus tip)

Sitting outside, I enjoyed watching the toddlers playing with each other in the courtyard, thinking about all those sweet yogurt pilgrims who had come before me, making today's treat possible.<//review><rating>5<//rating>< userid>

I can see how it can be longer but after seeing some reviews of 11 hours or more to unload I was very happy to get out sooner. They do allow you to go out and get food if needed with no issues. < Review>
Pizza Moda is great. I have a lot of food sensitivities, but ordering was no-hassle, and my food came out exactly as I'd ordered it. The waiter even suggested some good substitutions I didn't even think of.

They make house made vegan sausage, and you can do either Daiya or cashew cream as a vegan cheese. I asked for cashew cream on my pasta, which was delicious.

4 stars because we came in a large group and the service was slow (only one waiter for 25 people), but he was a nice guy, in any event.</Review>

< review>
I've heard Jeff the owner describe the restaurant as his "art project" and he treats it as such. The level of detail in the pizza moda experience truly elevates this from your normal pizza joint. Well thought out dec√≥r, a casual yet classy ambiance, carefully hidden accoustic treatment so even though the restaurant is lined with windows it doesn't get too loud unlike so many other places in town, attentive yet unrushed staff, a well thought out beverage selection (arrogant bastard on tap!), and of course Jeff tying it all together with his personnal touch. Our favorites from the regularly changing menu have been house smoked salmon pizza with pesto & caviar creme fraiche, fritto misto, and all the pastas have been to die for. Killer espresso, too!</review>

Three trips down the ladder later, the pan was dry again, but in order to alleviate any problems during the night we turned the A/C off and slept with our windows open and fans going. During this time, I had also made several calls to local places to see if anyone was available, but on a Sunday night ... no one was. Imagine that. Then I started doing what I do - due diligence and looking at reviews looking at costs and general overall reviews. After getting tired of spending too much on bottled water my wife and I decided to get a water purification system installed in our house. (May 2017) I LOVE the new system and my tap water now taste better than bottled water. We purchased a Puronics system.  Install was next day and seamless.

In early August I was out of town on business and my wife called me in panic because our AC was not working. We have a young toddler and it was 110 degrees outside. Not having AC was not an option. I remember that the experience we had with Environmental Heating and Air so I called around 5pm to see if they could look at my house ASAP. Matt, the owner, came by my house around 6:30pm and setup and delivered two portable AC units so my wife could put our son to bed. He checked my heating unit in the attic and saw that the drip pan was about to overflow. They drained my drip pan and after the technician did some test to see why it was failing. EHS replaced the capacitor tried to fix my old compressor, but it still failed. We decided to go with a new system. We chose the Lennox XC25-AC and SLP98 furnace. It is really nice to be able to adjust the temperature zones on our phone. The install was booked and installed two days later.

Now we have had TWO excellent experiences with EHA. To top it off last month they provided me with two club level tickets to the San Jose Sharks game! The tickets cam with free food, drinks and parking. EHA has exceeded all my expectations and has provided a great value. I would recommend them to a friend and would absolutely call them again if needed.</Text>
